    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_162607207" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/162607207" />
    <a title="Catie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1886642-catie"><img alt="Catie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1385169623p2/1886642.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/162607207?book_show_action=true">Apr 21, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Catie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Catie" href="/user/show/1886642-catie">Catie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=for-review">for-review</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer162607207" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17800473648007139452">This is the kind of book that I wish today’s teens would read. I don’t know how many times I’ve passive aggressively ranted in goodreads groups about the ridiculously unrealistic romances in the majority of young adult novels. I’m sure most of you know what I am referring to – instant, uncontrollable passion between two people who couldn’t be more one dimensional, combined with some manufactured reason that they can’t be together, and pages and pages of endless whinging about it. So this book, w</span>
  <span id="freeText17800473648007139452" style="display:none">This is the kind of book that I wish today’s teens would read. I don’t know how many times I’ve passive aggressively ranted in goodreads groups about the ridiculously unrealistic romances in the majority of young adult novels. I’m sure most of you know what I am referring to – instant, uncontrollable passion between two people who couldn’t be more one dimensional, combined with some manufactured reason that they can’t be together, and pages and pages of endless whinging about it. So this book, which is all about moving past romantic ideals and falling for the more complex truth, is quite refreshing.<br /><br />This story is told in alternating chapters by Lucy, Ed, and “Poet.” Through the course of one very long night, we follow Lucy as she tries to track down “Shadow” and “Poet,” two graffiti artists that she has been <s>stalking</s> following for quite some time. When Lucy’s friend Jazz becomes interested in tall, charming Leo, Lucy is forced to spend the night with Leo’s best friend Ed, with whom she shares an awkward past. Ed and Leo are heading into trouble, necessitated by Ed’s sudden unemployment and Leo’s debt to a very scary cockroach eating man and catalyzed by their mutual break ups. Lucy dreams of finding and connecting with Shadow, who she’s imagined into a perfect package. But, can she fall for thoughtful, quiet, Ed, whose standing right next to her?<br /><br />This book has a few elements that I’ve seen in other YA novels, but here they are accomplished with so much more heart and reality. Lucy’s parents are exactly what I kept hoping Mia’s parents would be in <u>If I Stay</u>. They are three dimensional, eccentric, artistic, loving parents who also argue and struggle financially, and are just human. Cath Crowley also manages to spin the “emo” poetry/art/music loving whiner guy into a real, self-conscious boy, who I really like! And actually, she does it twice! Lucy is a bit like a literary fangirl – she bases all of her assumptions about love and romance on her favorite books, and when asked to come up with a list of guys who she would “do it” with (by Jazz), she names all fictional characters. It’s very satisfying to see her journey to realization that love is very different from what she assumes, and so much better.<br /><br />There are a couple of things that I am not so sure about. The “villain” (a gangster that Leo is in debt to) really reminds me of one of those 80’s movie a-hole characters. You know, the slick, preppy, douche bag type guy? Except this version has about + 100 points of insanity. He does some violent things, but it kind of steps into the realm of “slapstick” in a way that makes me unsure of whether I am supposed to be laughing or cringing. I really wonder if this might be something that’s just lost in translation; apparently the U.S. version of this book will have some minor changes. In an interview with <a href="http://www.thetalescompendium.com" rel="nofollow noopener">The Tales Compendium</a>, Cath Crowley says,<br /><br /><i>”Graffiti Moon is essentially the same. There’s a little more about Ed’s mum, and a little less about Lucy’s parents. There are two more poems by Leo and a little more about Jazz. I really like the two of them so it was fun to add some more scenes.”</i><br /><br />(Note to U.S. editors – please help me understand if I am supposed to be laughing at the villain or running away in terror. Thanks.) <br /><br />Apparently, <u>Chasing Charlie Duskin</u> underwent some drastic changes before transforming into <u>A Little Wanting Song</u> for a U.S. audience (for instance, Charlie’s song lyrics only exist in the U.S. version!). So, I may be re-reading this when it comes to the U.S. just to see if I get the same reaction.<br /><br />I also didn’t like the poetry as much as I did in <u>A Little Wanting Song.</u> Although, I still think that Cath Crowley definitely has talent in that area. This is nowhere near some experiences I have had with prose authors attempting to add poetry into novels and failing miserably. She also really maintains the “teenage” feel to the poetry. It’s gorgeous, but just dramatic and awkward enough that I can fully believe that a teenager wrote it.<br /><br />This book is a light, funny, romantic read more than anything. (As another quick aside, I just want U.S. YA authors to take note: it is in fact possible to write a light read that includes serious topics like death, poverty, and divorce, and includes young people struggling through life. This book is evidence. So please stop centering all light reads around wealthy kids with every advantage. Thank you.) It reminds me a bit of John Green or David Levithan, and I think that it will appeal to quite a lot of people. I normally like my books to be a bit on the darker side, but the main theme of this one is so near and dear to my heart that I am giving it four stars.<br /><br />I think that I should add that this book also contains a lot of art references. I am not very knowledgeable about art, but I did enjoy looking up images of some of the pieces that are mentioned. However, I know that this will not appeal to everyone, so fair warning!<br /><br /><u>Perfect Musical Pairing</u><br /><br />Tegan and Sara – <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Va9uOHGZskg&amp;feature=related&lt;br%20/&gt;" rel="nofollow noopener">Call It Off</a> <br /><br />Twins Tegan and Sara Quin can so effortlessly capture raw longing with their bare, harmonizing voices. This song is such an emotional ode to missed chances and I think that it’s the perfect complement to <u>Graffiti Moon</u>. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17800473648007139452" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_203888838" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/203888838" />
    <a title="Noelle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2448124-noelle"><img alt="Noelle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1492692932p2/2448124.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/203888838?book_show_action=true">Aug 31, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Noelle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Noelle" href="/user/show/2448124-noelle">Noelle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780375983658" href="/book/show/12418474-graffiti-moon">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2448124-noelle?shelf=on-my-literal-bookshelf">on-my-literal-bookshelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2448124-noelle?shelf=forever-and-ever-amen">forever-and-ever-amen</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2448124-noelle?shelf=2011-favorites">2011-favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer203888838" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3714328153151378375">I just loved this book. Loooooved it. I've already re-read it several times and as I mentioned in another review, it's pretty much spray painted on my heart. (See what I did there???? BUT IT'S TRUE!) Obviously, this deserved a more in-depth review.<br/><br/>I loved the protagonists. Lucy is naive but no pushover. I cracked up when it was revealed that her list of people she’d like to “do it” with was entirely comprised of fictional characters. Remember that age of having a crush on someone that you hardly</span>
  <span id="freeText3714328153151378375" style="display:none">I just loved this book. Loooooved it. I've already re-read it several times and as I mentioned in another review, it's pretty much spray painted on my heart. (See what I did there???? BUT IT'S TRUE!) Obviously, this deserved a more in-depth review.<br><br>I loved the protagonists. Lucy is naive but no pushover. I cracked up when it was revealed that her list of people she’d like to “do it” with was entirely comprised of fictional characters. Remember that age of having a crush on someone that you hardly knew, the basis of who you had made up almost entirely in your head? Never mind that you never actually talked to this guy. The very impossibility of anything happening with him was the most comforting part! It was more fun to imagine love in abstract rather than experience the messy, frightening reality of getting to actually know and care for a real, flawed person. And I mean, who wants to deal with the reality of a high school boy? They are just about custom-made as you can get to disillusion the crap out of any romantic ideals.<br><br>And that brings us to Ed, a boy betrayed by words and saved by art. He doesn't seem to have a lot going on at first glance but given the chance, revealed delightfully unexpected depths. For all of Lucy’s romanticizing and idealizing, I thought Ed was pretty romantic at heart. I think there’s something inherently romantic about creating art and not just in the creation of something heartfelt, or the visual representation of emotions. It doesn’t matter the subject matter. Art can be as fanciful, impractical and unrealistic as you (the artist or viewer) want. It can <i>mean</i> whatever you want. It has endless possibility. But more than anything, art is expressing a true self. And what’s more romantic than that?<br><br>I thought <i>Graffiti Moon</i> perfectly captured the moment where the breathless exhilaration of youth and possibility collides with "real world" gravity establishing its weight. I loved the undercurrent of yearning and the theme of self-expression. I loved how it was bittersweet, naive, hopeful and absolutely hysterical. The banter and dialogue were particularly enchanting.<br><br><i>"For a while, for as long as you're looking at it, that painting is the world and you get to be in it."</i> To me, <i>Graffiti Moon</i> was that work of art, and what a pleasure it was to spend time in it's world.<br><br><u>Some odds and ends:</u><br><br>• After reading this, I started a <i>Graffiti Moon</i>-inspired painting, that's how much I loved it. I'm still messing with it here and there but in honor of the US release date, here it is. I called it <i>I Want to Collide</i> (but of course! :D):<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1438423609i/15704807.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>• Make sure to check out this awesome link of all the art mentions in <i>Graffiti Moon</i> at <a href="http://www.persnicketysnark.com/2011/11/graffiti-moon-art-gallery.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Persnickety Snark</a><br><br>• An example of Cath Crowley's pure amazingness:<br><blockquote>
  <i>"She sounds smart." I try to make that comment seem casual but weirdly, anything I say about Beth comes out of my mouth dressed in a full-length ball gown.</i>
</blockquote><br><br><br><i>This is a review of the Australian edition of this book.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="3714328153151378375" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_116082608" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/116082608" />
    <a title="Nic" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2813423-nic"><img alt="Nic" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/116082608?book_show_action=true">Aug 10, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nic" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nic" href="/user/show/2813423-nic">Nic</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2813423-nic?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2813423-nic?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2813423-nic?shelf=swoon-worthy-read">swoon-worthy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2813423-nic?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2813423-nic?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2813423-nic?shelf=aussie-ya">aussie-ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer116082608" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16743794227245836749"><i>"For a while, for as long as you're looking at it, that painting is the world and you get to be in it."</i><br/><br/>I decided to give Graffiti Moon a try after reading my Goodreads friend Nomes' review. And I am so glad I did because it was brilliant! <br/><br/>The story is written in both Lucy’s and Ed’s point of view. You have got to love dual narration where you get into both character's minds. There is also some poetry from Poet (Shadow‘s friend) thrown in as well just to mix it up a bit more. And despite all thes</span>
  <span id="freeText16743794227245836749" style="display:none"><i>"For a while, for as long as you're looking at it, that painting is the world and you get to be in it."</i><br /><br />I decided to give Graffiti Moon a try after reading my Goodreads friend Nomes' review. And I am so glad I did because it was brilliant! <br /><br />The story is written in both Lucy’s and Ed’s point of view. You have got to love dual narration where you get into both character's minds. There is also some poetry from Poet (Shadow‘s friend) thrown in as well just to mix it up a bit more. And despite all these elements it never gets confusing or feels like the author is repeating herself. The writing has lyrical feel to it and Crowley definitely has a way with words. The way she described the art in the story I felt like I was standing there looking at it and I wish I was. So beautifully descriptive. The plot was set over the course of one night and it was fast paced and had plenty of surprises. I think the cover describes the plot the so well "an artist, a dreamer, a long, mean night". <br /><br />Crowley writes vibrant and believable characters. Lucy, I liked instantly. She was smart but also a dreamer and wasn’t afraid to break a guy nose if he deserves it. Ed is definitely a crush worthy character although I wasn’t sure at first. But underneath that troublemaker image is a sweet guy with a beautiful artistic soul that doesn’t realise his own self worth. Lucy and Ed had plenty of witty banter and loads of chemistry. There also was lots of funny moments provided by a great mix of secondary characters. <br /><br />Overall a clever, funny and heartfelt story. The only problem is I did not want this story to end! </span>
  <a data-text-id="16743794227245836749" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_903691769" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/903691769" />
    <a title="Kaya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15462098-kaya"><img alt="Kaya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1485382914p2/15462098.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/903691769?book_show_action=true">Apr 07, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaya" href="/user/show/15462098-kaya">Kaya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer903691769" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11867752992052310425">This is a sweet, light novel, a little bit shallow and naive. Or maybe it's about time for me to accept the fact that I'm too selective when it comes to YA books. I didn't like our protagonists. Lucy was obnoxious and Ed was passive. Leo's poems were also a downfall. I suppose simple story about young love isn't enough for me anymore. <br/><br/>The book is about one night of adventure, risky bicycle rides and different types of confrontation and confessions. It's about art, poetry, and misunderstandings. </span>
  <span id="freeText11867752992052310425" style="display:none">This is a sweet, light novel, a little bit shallow and naive. Or maybe it's about time for me to accept the fact that I'm too selective when it comes to YA books. I didn't like our protagonists. Lucy was obnoxious and Ed was passive. Leo's poems were also a downfall. I suppose simple story about young love isn't enough for me anymore. <br /><br />The book is about one night of adventure, risky bicycle rides and different types of confrontation and confessions. It's about art, poetry, and misunderstandings. Taking place in one night in Melbourne, the story is told in different perspectives of Lucy, Ed and Leo's dull poems. It starts out with Lucy pedalling on her bike to see Shadow, a Graffiti artist whose works she's obsessed with. Lucy thinks Shadow is her prince on a white horse and when she gets there she misses him by five minutes. <br /><br />Later on, she meets her friends Jazz and Daisy and they spend the night out to celebrate the end of high school. Jazz assumes she's a psychic and it's so repetitive I wanted to smack her down multiple times. The girls hang out with Ed, Leo and Dylan at the same place. Daisy and Dylan have been dating for two years and they go through a rough patch. Jazz and Leo start flirting, which leaves Lucy with Ed. They went out once few years ago and she literally broke his nose and left him bleeding because he touched her ass. Ed tells Lucy he knows where to find Shadow and Poet and then the whole gang goes to find them. <br /><br />As a book, this is only ok, but I think it would've made a great movie. What Graffiti Moon lacks the most is witty dialogue and penetrating background. It didn't raise any emotions, being so boring at times. It really is only for high school readers. The story gives nothing new to the genre and is very predictable. About halfway through the story I predicted the ending and I wasn't wrong. Leo's poems served no purpose, they were just there to make him likeable which didn't succeed obviously. Though, all characters are really passionate about art. <br /><br /><b>I</b> also didn't like frequent switching of viewpoints because both Ed and Lucy sounded alike. I often have forgotten who was who because their voices sounded the same. There was a lot of repetition of dialogues when switching points of view and that was extremely pointless. Basically, this book is about spending the night out with your friends and your friend's boyfriend's friends whom you barely know and to make them go around the city in the hopes of finding two guys (Shadow and Poet) you only know because of their graffiti. If one of my friends suggested something like that, I'd instantly go home. <br /><br />Lucy is a classical judgemental, prudish and two-dimensional YA heroine. She has nothing to offer to the readers because she acts like a five year old, but expects others to treat her like she's an adult. Ugh, I seriously don't understand what Ed likes about her. Someone needed to put some sense into her.<br /><br />Ed was a bit more compelling, but still failed to be an interesting narrator. All he did was brood about how his life sucks. Fine, if you're not happy with your life, fucking do something about it and stop complaining. Yes, I know he's 18, but if he wants to be independent, he better starts acting like it. <br /><br />Our main characters meet in the first few chapters, but they hate each other. Lucy doesn’t know Ed is actually Shadow and dismisses him as a jerk. Ed isn't aware of Lucy's obsession with Shadow and is still upset over what happened on their date years ago. Most of the time, their bond was kind of flat, but I still ended up rooting for them.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11867752992052310425" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_151550456" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/151550456" />
    <a title="~Tina~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2594672-tina"><img alt="~Tina~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1411474324p2/2594672.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/151550456?book_show_action=true">Mar 02, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="~Tina~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="~Tina~" href="/user/show/2594672-tina">~Tina~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780375869532" href="/book/show/11387507-graffiti-moon">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=read-2011">read-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=netgalley-edelweiss">netgalley-edelweiss</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer151550456" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4809415937164175741"><a href='http://irresistiblereads.blogspot.com/p/aussie-ya-reading-challenge-2011.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Aussie Book challenge</a> 2011 #9<br/><br/>Okay! I definitely hate myself since I really had no intention of reading this book (insert gasp here). I don't favor contemporary much, but being that a lot of my friends have read and raved about this and it being an Aussie book (nuff said) I decided to just give it a shot, and boy was I thrilled and surprised how much I truly loved this.<br/><br/>I absolutely fell in love with every single one of these characters! <br/>Ed and Lucy, Leo and Jazz and even Dylan and Daisy. Each are</span>
  <span id="freeText4809415937164175741" style="display:none"><a href="http://irresistiblereads.blogspot.com/p/aussie-ya-reading-challenge-2011.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Aussie Book challenge</a> 2011 #9<br /><br />Okay! I definitely hate myself since I really had no intention of reading this book (insert gasp here). I don't favor contemporary much, but being that a lot of my friends have read and raved about this and it being an Aussie book (nuff said) I decided to just give it a shot, and boy was I thrilled and surprised how much I truly loved this.<br /><br />I absolutely fell in love with every single one of these characters! <br />Ed and Lucy, Leo and Jazz and even Dylan and Daisy. Each are extremely well written, complex and a total blast to read. But my favorite characters would have to go out to Ed and Leo. I love there tight 'you go I go' friendship and how they have each others backs and how they each have unique gifts that they share in common ways. <br />How freaken cute are Ed and Lucy? I loved how he ended up being the guy Lucy went out with a couple years back. I loved that they got their second chance, even if they didn't know it at the time. I adore how Ed feels so much and love the way he expresses it. Lucy is just to adorable for words. She's sweet and feisty and feels just as much as Ed, but doesn't hold back. Also, you got to love a protag that can break a boys nose. You just do. <br />Ed and Lucy's night searching for Shadow was like reading in 3D. I could vividly picture ever wall and every feeling that went into that piece. I simply adore how each one is explained by a memory or conversation. It really gave me a wonderful connection with who Ed really was and how Lucy saw each impression. Same goes for Leo's words and I love the reason behind why he needed the money and the fact that he's a bit scared of his Gran. Respect;)<br /><br />As for the writing? It really is it's own brilliant piece of art. I've read Cath Crowley <i>A Little Wanting Song</i> and I had to admit I was shocked that this was the same author. I liked that book just fine, but <i>this</i> book is a masterpiece. From the moment I read the very first line, I was totally invested in these characters. I loved loved the humor, the flirtatious banter and easy fit wit. I love that there are intense moments but it didn't overwhelm me, just made me want to read this as fast as I could and savor it at the same time. <br /><br />All in all, I absolutely adored this book, in fact, it's going down as one of the best reads in 2011 and an instant favorite. I can't wait till this book hits the shelves!<br />I am not an artist in any shape or form. I can't draw, I can't play music, sing or dance and I am no writer. But...I am a huge art lover. <b>Graffiti Moon</b> is art my friends, in the best, surprising way possible!<br /><br />Smart, infectious and completely absorbing. Everyone needs to read this Outstanding gem! <br /><br />(Arc provided by Netgalley and Random House Children's Books)<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4809415937164175741" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_279413448" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/279413448" />
    <a title="Giselle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4800103-giselle"><img alt="Giselle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1310159877p2/4800103.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/279413448?book_show_action=true">Feb 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Giselle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Giselle" href="/user/show/4800103-giselle">Giselle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780375869532" href="/book/show/11387507-graffiti-moon">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4800103-giselle?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4800103-giselle?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer279413448" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11513724208750283222">I know nothing about graffiti, I know even less about art - why the heck did I read this book? Well, for the same reason you should! It's an incredibly sweet, delightfully romantic story that can <i>not</i> be on your unread shelf. Why?<br/>    -True to life, complex romance<br/>    -Artistic imagery that will enthrall any reader- art fanatic or not<br/>    -Characters that make you fall in love<br/>    -A story that is simply too gorgeous to be left unexplored<br/><br/>If this isn't enough to convince you, maybe you should go back</span>
  <span id="freeText11513724208750283222" style="display:none">I know nothing about graffiti, I know even less about art - why the heck did I read this book? Well, for the same reason you should! It's an incredibly sweet, delightfully romantic story that can <i>not</i> be on your unread shelf. Why?<br />    -True to life, complex romance<br />    -Artistic imagery that will enthrall any reader- art fanatic or not<br />    -Characters that make you fall in love<br />    -A story that is simply too gorgeous to be left unexplored<br /><br />If this isn't enough to convince you, maybe you should go back to playing with Legos.<br /><br />I must admit, I did not get into the story right away. I don't know if it was the unique lyrical writing, or the artsy details, but I kept getting distracted. The writing, although beautiful, is much more elaborate than what I was expecting from a young-adult novel so it threw me off at first. However, once I got into it, I couldn't stop staring at these beautiful sentences that simply blew me away. Or these outstanding characters that do nothing less than take your heart, and pull you inside the pages.<br /><br />Lucy is desperate to find this graffiti artist who calls himself Shadow. Ed is a lost soul who paints to find himself. We're taken into this story with a dual perspective that lets us see into each of these characters hearts; these characters who are notably profound, yet believable. I loved how they aren't stylized to fit the unconvincing image of prim and proper teenagers we often get in YA novels. These are real, raw personalities who express themselves with art, while trying to find their place in this big, unforgiving world. Cath does not soften the edges to make a cute, romantic story, she gives us a story so pure, so deep, that it bleeds out the truest of love stories.<br /><br />There is a lot more in here than a love story, however. We see these kids struggle through real life problems - financial dilemmas, marital issues and death are all a part of this well rounded tale. It's undoubtedly a one of a kind novel that is bound to impress a wide range of readers, from young to adult. I'm glad that, despite my lack of artistic knowledge, I decided to give this one a try- and you should too! <br /><br />--<br />For more of my reviews, visit my blog at <a href="http://www.xpressoreads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <b>Xpresso Reads</b>
</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="11513724208750283222" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer183325049" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14859465548301351244">This review can also be found at <a href='http://the-book-eater.blogspot.com/2011/04/review-saving-francesca-by-melina.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <u>The Book Eater</u>
</a><br/><br/><b>ATTN READING MANIACS AND BOOK LOVERS:</b> To all of you who have regular reading slumps, READ THIS. I can guarantee this book will get you out of it.<br/><br/>So, I finished this book 4 days ago and I'm still trying to gather my thoughts into coherent sentences.<br/>The writing was so beautiful that I kept stopping to stare at the words. I wanted to crawl across the page and come up to the words and snuggle them. And also hug the characters.<br/>This is the kind of boo</span>
  <span id="freeText14859465548301351244" style="display:none">This review can also be found at <a href="http://the-book-eater.blogspot.com/2011/04/review-saving-francesca-by-melina.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <u>The Book Eater</u>
</a><br /><br /><b>ATTN READING MANIACS AND BOOK LOVERS:</b> To all of you who have regular reading slumps, READ THIS. I can guarantee this book will get you out of it.<br /><br />So, I finished this book 4 days ago and I'm still trying to gather my thoughts into coherent sentences.<br />The writing was so beautiful that I kept stopping to stare at the words. I wanted to crawl across the page and come up to the words and snuggle them. And also hug the characters.<br />This is the kind of book that puts a huge smile on your face. The kind of book that makes your day better. Hell, it makes your day, period.<br />The storyline was realistic and lovely, the characters had depth and personalities, the banter was perfect and I just wish I could take a swim in this novel and never come out. And hug the characters. Always hug the characters.<br /><br />I do hope the author will make some kind of companion novel to Graffiti Moon. She has more than enough talent to pull it off, and honestly, I'm not ready to say goodbye to these folks quite yet. I'd even want to read the parents' story (they're actually multi-dimensional! And <i>interesting</i>!) I don't care. JUST WRITE MORE.<br /><br />I would recommend this book to anyone, anybody who loves good writing and lovable characters. It's right up there with Saving Francesca and the likes. And if you don't trust me, trust the judging panel of this year's Australian Prime Minister's Literary Awards. Graffiti Moon won the first prize in the "Young adult fiction" category. Yup. Go read now.</span>

<div id="review_198068990" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/198068990" />
    <a title="Maggie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4222084-maggie"><img alt="Maggie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1319666686p2/4222084.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/198068990?book_show_action=true">Aug 13, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maggie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maggie" href="/user/show/4222084-maggie">Maggie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780375869532" href="/book/show/11387507-graffiti-moon">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4222084-maggie?shelf=aussie-aussie-aussie-oi-oi-oi">aussie-aussie-aussie-oi-oi-oi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4222084-maggie?shelf=2012">2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4222084-maggie?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4222084-maggie?shelf=i-ve-just-read-you-and-i-love-you">i-ve-just-read-you-and-i-love-you</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4222084-maggie?shelf=crushworthy-guys">crushworthy-guys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4222084-maggie?shelf=a-z-book-2012">a-z-book-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4222084-maggie?shelf=aussie-2012">aussie-2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer198068990" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9751339475384892458"><i>Art is a human activity consisting in this, that one man consciously, by means of certain external signs, hands on to others feelings he has lived through, and that other people are infected by these feelings and also experience them.</i><br/>—The <i>other</i> Leo, Leo Tolstoy<br/><br/>You know, if my high school teacher had just handed me <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7863274.Graffiti_Moon' title='Graffiti Moon by Cath Crowley' rel='nofollow noopener'>Graffiti Moon</a> to explain aesthetics, Tolstoy and Kant would've made so much more sense. And been so much more enjoyable.<br/><br/>What can I say about <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1348627.Cath_Crowley' title='Cath Crowley' rel='nofollow noopener'>Cath Crowley</a> and this book that Tolstoy has</span>
  <span id="freeText9751339475384892458" style="display:none"><i>Art is a human activity consisting in this, that one man consciously, by means of certain external signs, hands on to others feelings he has lived through, and that other people are infected by these feelings and also experience them.</i><br>—The <i>other</i> Leo, Leo Tolstoy<br><br>You know, if my high school teacher had just handed me <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7863274.Graffiti_Moon" title="Graffiti Moon by Cath Crowley" rel="nofollow noopener">Graffiti Moon</a> to explain aesthetics, Tolstoy and Kant would've made so much more sense. And been so much more enjoyable.<br><br>What can I say about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1348627.Cath_Crowley" title="Cath Crowley" rel="nofollow noopener">Cath Crowley</a> and this book that Tolstoy hasn't? How about I show you how people have been infected by her feelings and experienced them. <br><br><blockquote>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/203888838" rel="nofollow noopener">Noelle</a> did a painting inspired by Graffiti Moon after reading it.<br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/203888838" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380356833i/708260.jpg" width="250" height="253" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br>Click on the picture to see a larger version in her review. I'm still harasking (not a typo) her to make prints.<br><br>A Sharon Hayes made this video:<br><a target="_blank" href="http://animoto.com/play/RppbqfnqI6gNIK8EjDgITA" rel="nofollow noopener"><span>[image error]</span></a><br>Video featured in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/174262009" rel="nofollow noopener">Ari's fantastic review</a>
</blockquote><br>Graffiti Moon is art. It takes you along as it follows Lucy and Ed on the last night of high school, but it's also about their relationship with Ed's secret alter ego, Shadow, the guy who paints in the dark. Lucy doesn't know who he is, but she knows enough about him from the pieces of himself he leaves around the city via his paintings. Ed is... lost. Except when he's Shadow. As Ed, he's just lost his job, his boss/mentor/confidant, his girlfriend, and his direction. One thing Lucy and Ed have in common, aside from Shadow, is their art. Lucy is learning to be a glass blower from her own boss/mentor/confidant, and she's as good in her art as Shadow is in his. Through their friends, Lucy and Ed end up thrown together despite their mutual reluctance. The reason for that reluctance is classic Crowley. (See <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3165049-the-life-and-times-of-gracie-faltrain" rel="nofollow noopener">Faltrain, Gracie</a>.)<br><br>I knew I loved Lucy from the moment she tells off a guy with, "You don't do that on a first date. Atticus Finch would never have done that." My girl! And she has parents who say things like,<br><blockquote>Mum laughs. “We raised a very conservative daughter. Too much Pride and Prejudice.”<br><br>“That could change,” Dad says. “There’s still time to get her onto Margaret Atwood.”</blockquote>How is it that I simultaneously want to be the daughter and the parent in this situation?<br><br>And Ed. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7417780-the-piper-s-son" rel="nofollow noopener">Tom Mackee</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1162022.On_the_Jellicoe_Road" rel="nofollow noopener">Jonah Griggs</a>, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4374400-if-i-stay" rel="nofollow noopener">Adam Wilde</a> would like to welcome you into the book crush hall of fame. <br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380356833i/708262.png" width="400" height="98" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote>Leo/Poet is right there too. Lucy's description of Leo in the Australian edition nearly, very nearly, made me forget about Ed for a second.<br><blockquote>I once saw him from a distance and thought a tree was strolling towards me. An oak tree with a shaved head, soft eyes, and a tattoo.</blockquote>Perhaps that's why they chose to leave that little snippet out of the US edition, which brings me to my next topic.<br><br><u>Cultural Differences Between Australians and Americans as Evidenced in YA Literature</u> <i>Class to be taught by Professor Crowley at the University of In Our Dreams at a date TBD</i><br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/277551079" rel="nofollow noopener">Catie</a> does a brilliant job of breaking down the Aussie vs US editions in her <a href="http://www.thereadventurer.com/1/post/2012/02/ya-review-graffiti-moon-by-cath-crowley.html" rel="nofollow noopener">post at The Readventurer</a>. To piggyback on her discussion, the main thing I noticed based on what was cut vs what was added in the US version is that Australians are rock 'n roll and Americans are emo. Rolling Stones "I can't get no..." references cut! Alanis Morissette reference added. My notes had a giant "MEH!" here. Also, the noble single mother goes down very well with an American audience. Whereas Ed's mum was a figure in the Aussie edition, she is now a PRESENCE in the US edition. Ed's absentee father also gets a bigger role in the US edition with his absence. Ed wonders about what kind of legacy his father has left for him by leaving. These things don't detract from the story at all. In fact, I think most audiences would embrace Ed's struggles. <i>However</i>, having read the Aussie edition first and loving that story as it was presented, it felt unnecessary to me.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380356833ra/708263.gif" width="480" height="203" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Still, I can't hate on the US edition when one of the added lines is one I absolutely love:<br><blockquote>“I know that,” I say, trying to act like I’m not embarrassed for thinking love and sex are the same thing. I know they’re not, but I want them to be close enough to at least brush each other as they pass.</blockquote>The US edition also has two new poems by Leo, which is a nice bonus.<br><br>Regardless of which edition you have, you're good. If George Lucas can come out with 125 editions of Star Wars, Cath Crowley can have 2 editions of her books. Like the Star Wars geeks I can never make fun of again, I found myself ordering the Australian version, the US version, and today, the audiobook version. I may not be able to express my love for this book by painting, but I can do it by shopping! </span>
  <a data-text-id="9751339475384892458" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_117340124" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/117340124" />
    <a title="Alexa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1894085-alexa"><img alt="Alexa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1393730599p2/1894085.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/117340124?book_show_action=true">Aug 17, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alexa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alexa" href="/user/show/1894085-alexa">Alexa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780375869532" href="/book/show/11387507-graffiti-moon">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1894085-alexa?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1894085-alexa?shelf=2011-reads">2011-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1894085-alexa?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1894085-alexa?shelf=to-buy">to-buy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1894085-alexa?shelf=aussie">aussie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1894085-alexa?shelf=tour">tour</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer117340124" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9246892416262044829"><br/>My review can also be found on my blog <a href='http://collections-books.blogspot.com/2011/07/review-graffiti-moon-by-cath-crowley.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Collections</a>.<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380338544i/695582.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
  <br/>
  <i>"...we watch the dirty silk of the factory smoke float across the sky."</i>
</blockquote>I loved that there was a lot of graffiti and mentions of glassblowing in <i>Graffiti Moon</i>. Photographs of urban decay featuring old, abandoned buildings and factories are my favorite form of art to look at, but graffiti is a close second. Whenever I see graffiti sprayed on the wall of a building or painted on the side of a boxcar moving along the railroad tracks, I alw</span>
  <span id="freeText9246892416262044829" style="display:none"><br>My review can also be found on my blog <a href="http://collections-books.blogspot.com/2011/07/review-graffiti-moon-by-cath-crowley.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Collections</a>.<br><br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380338544i/695582.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  <br>
  <i>"...we watch the dirty silk of the factory smoke float across the sky."</i>
</blockquote>I loved that there was a lot of graffiti and mentions of glassblowing in <i>Graffiti Moon</i>. Photographs of urban decay featuring old, abandoned buildings and factories are my favorite form of art to look at, but graffiti is a close second. Whenever I see graffiti sprayed on the wall of a building or painted on the side of a boxcar moving along the railroad tracks, I always wonder, <i>'Who made that? When did they do it? Why did they do it? And where are they now?</i>' It just blows my mind, and it's one of the reasons why I loved this book.<br><br>Lucy wonders about the graffiti made by the artist who calls himself Shadow. She finds Shadow's work to be extremely inspiring, and she is determined to figure out his identity so that she can meet him in person. She wants to tell him everything she feels whenever she sees his work...and what she feels for him because of it. But she's been searching for Shadow for awhile now and it seems she misses him by mere minutes every single time. Then one night, Lucy and her friends meet a few guys from school who claim to know Shadow. One of the guys is Ed, someone she has a history with and doesn't want to be around. But she's willing to endure Ed's company for the night if hanging out with him means finally meeting Shadow.<br><br>I have read one other book by Cath Crowley (<i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7124053.A_Little_Wanting_Song" title="A Little Wanting Song by Cath Crowley" rel="nofollow noopener">A Little Wanting Song</a>
</i>, which I loved!), and she has already made my favorite authors list. I absolutely love her writing. Her characters are extremely likable and funny, and they have such great relationships. I could easily relate to Lucy, and she was spunky and just completely awesome. Ed... I adored him. I want my own Ed. Lucy seems to have gotten the wrong impression of him because I think he's actually the kind of guy you <i>want</i> to be around. In the book, Ed takes Lucy on an adventure through the city to see more of Shadow's graffiti. I thought the atmosphere and the setting were perfect. It made me want to be there with them, hanging out and exploring the city at night in search of amazing graffiti.<br><br>Like I mentioned, I always have questions whenever I see graffiti, and I felt Lucy and I shared the same curiosity. Who is this mysterious guy who fills her with so much inspiration? And where is he? Since <i>Graffiti Moon</i> is told in alternating point of views between Lucy and Ed, Shadow's real identity is quite obvious to the readers. However, I didn't feel it lessened the mystery or allure of Shadow, especially since Lucy truly has no idea. I always wonder if someone will live up to my expectations when I meet them, and for Lucy it's even more crucial because she's falling for Shadow. I was holding my breath for the moment when Lucy finally figures out who he is. Will he be like the Shadow she's imagined? Or will she end up being disappointed? I think moments like that are pretty priceless. <br><br>I cannot wait to read more novels by Cath Crowley because this was another book that I didn't want to end. I highly recommend <i>Graffiti Moon</i> to YA contemporary and Aussie fans. If you can't get a hold of this book and you desperately want to read it, don't worry. It will be published in the US on February 14, 2012 from Knopf Books for Young Readers. The cover is amazing, by the way. Be sure to check it out!<br><br><br>(Note: The factory picture is by <a href="http://fav.me/d24gim5" rel="nofollow noopener">PET</a>.)</span>
  <a data-text-id="9246892416262044829" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_210287637" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/210287637" />
    <a title="♥Rachel♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5481477-rachel"><img alt="♥Rachel♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1363996055p2/5481477.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/210287637?book_show_action=true">Sep 18, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="♥Rachel♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="♥Rachel♥" href="/user/show/5481477-rachel">♥Rachel♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780375983658" href="/book/show/12418474-graffiti-moon">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5481477-rachel?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5481477-rachel?shelf=netgalley-e-book">netgalley-e-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5481477-rachel?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5481477-rachel?shelf=aussie-books">aussie-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5481477-rachel?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer210287637" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11439591780422044424">I loved this story! I didn't want it to end. <br/><br/>The story of Graffiti Moon takes place over twenty-four hours. Lucy is a seventeen-year old student who's just finished year twelve and is out for the night with her friends to celebrate. Her whole focus for the evening is to find Shadow, a graffiti artist that does these amazing heartfelt paintings all over the city. She feels a powerful connection to these paintings, and the emotion behind them. Lucy has a passion for art and thinks whoever Shadow i</span>
  <span id="freeText11439591780422044424" style="display:none">I loved this story! I didn't want it to end. <br /><br />The story of Graffiti Moon takes place over twenty-four hours. Lucy is a seventeen-year old student who's just finished year twelve and is out for the night with her friends to celebrate. Her whole focus for the evening is to find Shadow, a graffiti artist that does these amazing heartfelt paintings all over the city. She feels a powerful connection to these paintings, and the emotion behind them. Lucy has a passion for art and thinks whoever Shadow is, he's the one for her. I loved this quote, from Lucy on Shadow: <br /><br /><i>I want to collide. I want to run right into Shadow and let the force spill our thoughts so we can pick each other up and pass each other back like piles of shiny stones.</i><br /><br />So Lucy meets up with her friends Jazz and Daisy to have an all-nighter of fun. They quickly run into Ed, Leo, and Dylan a group of friends from school. Dylan is sort of Daisy's boyfriend who idea of romance is throwing eggs on her head. <i>Surprisingly</i>, Daisy doesn’t consider this a romantic gesture, and so is currently on the outs with him. Lucy has her own history with Ed, so she's not to keen on hanging out with him but Jazz is definitely keen on Leo. Plus, Leo and Dylan claim to know who Shadow and Poet are, so they could spend the night looking for them at all their haunts. So Lucy agrees to this night with the promise of finally tracking down the boy of her dreams. (Forgot to mention Poet always pens a little something with each painting so they're known as a duo: Shadow and Poet). So this is how the adventure begins. <br /><br />This story was so lovely with all the descriptions of art, from Lucy's glass blowing to Shadows paintings, you felt like you were really seeing them through your mind's eye. One of my favorite of Shadows pieces is of "a heart cracked by earthquake with the words <i>Beyond the Richter scale</i> written underneath." This story is told alternating from Ed and Lucy's POV, and I guess there's also a POV of Poet in there because every few chapters you get pieces of poetry from him (which are amazing). I'm a big fan of alternate POVs, I loved getting both Lucy and Ed's thoughts throughout. Lucy was an amazing main character, spunky and determined, full of heart. You got to love a girl who's not afraid to bash a boy in the nose when required. Ed, I'm in love with you! You are definitely on my list of book boyfriends. He's a thinker, lover-of-art, full of witty and smart conversation. I loved the banter with these two, the push and pull was so much fun. As if all of this wasn't enough to love this story, there are some scenes that had me laughing to the point of crying. The bicycle scene in the park was priceless. This book is a must read! I received this through Netgalley, but I'm buying my own copy so that I can hold it in my hands, and know it's on my shelf, to re-read anytime I want! <br /><br /><i>Thank you to Netgalley and Random House for allowing me to read this amazing story!</i><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11439591780422044424" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_198417572" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/198417572" />
    <a title="Cara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1876075-cara"><img alt="Cara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350665534p2/1876075.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/198417572?book_show_action=true">Aug 14, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cara" href="/user/show/1876075-cara">Cara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780375869532" href="/book/show/11387507-graffiti-moon">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1876075-cara?shelf=male-protagonist">male-protagonist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1876075-cara?shelf=awesome-covers">awesome-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1876075-cara?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1876075-cara?shelf=2012">2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer198417572" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18173302134153918695">Ah I loved it. What a beautiful atmosphere and eclectic characters that I couldn't help but like. I know this may seem odd but I thought I wasn't going to love it as much as other people did. I was <i>completely</i> wrong.<br/><br/>Ed is Shadow, the local graffiti artist. His best friend Leo is Poet and does the writing. Lucy is a glassblower. Her best friend Jazz is psychic. Then there is the odd, complicated, adorable couple of Daisy and Dylan. One night these people meet up to celebrate the end of year twelve</span>
  <span id="freeText18173302134153918695" style="display:none">Ah I loved it. What a beautiful atmosphere and eclectic characters that I couldn't help but like. I know this may seem odd but I thought I wasn't going to love it as much as other people did. I was <i>completely</i> wrong.<br /><br />Ed is Shadow, the local graffiti artist. His best friend Leo is Poet and does the writing. Lucy is a glassblower. Her best friend Jazz is psychic. Then there is the odd, complicated, adorable couple of Daisy and Dylan. One night these people meet up to celebrate the end of year twelve. What ensues is the hunt for Shadow, a pink get away van, threats of nipple piercings, and copious amounts of near embarrassing/interesting incidents. <br /><br />The book shows teenagers in a realistic way. Flawed but hopeful. Animated but at the same time philosophical. Melodramatic but idealistic. It's complicated being a teenager but with the right group of people it can be great. I knew when I was reading it that it was set for only one night but it certainly feels longer than that. I felt like I knew the characters enough to understand why they did things, and was crossing my fingers for them. The “specialness” of the night can be felt, and it's filled with a buzzing anticipation. A climatic event is bound to happen. <br /><br />The author is almost pitch perfect with her word choices. The dialogue has the right amount of bite but realism to it. I caught myself visualizing all of Shadow's art, and then found myself wishing it existed in real life. I loved how the story was not only narrated between Lucy and Ed, but also with Leo's poems. Actually out of the bunch he was my favorite character. Then there is that cover! What a unique and eye-catching mix of colors contrasting with the black and white. Perfect for this story.<br /><br />I wish I had a nice way to end the review but I really don't. I loved it and I think that's gonna have to be enough.<br /><br /><b>Extra side story: </b>I have a story of why I was so impressed with this novel. First off (please don't hate me after I write this) I am not an art person. I took an Art History course a couple of semesters back and I <u>hated</u> it. It was probably the most boring class I have taken in college. As a class we had to take a trip to an art museum. I had no fun and to be honest I was kind of miserable for the whole trip. I saw the other students who were taking the class as part of their major and they were just enthralled and excited. I didn't get it, especially for the abstract pieces. But I'm betting if I were with Ed or Lucy I would have. The art popped out to me and I caught the bug. I got what the big deal was.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18173302134153918695" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_182735361" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/182735361" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4844873-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1299680097p2/4844873.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/182735361?book_show_action=true">Jul 07, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/4844873-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780375869532" href="/book/show/11387507-graffiti-moon">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4844873-laura?shelf=for-one-night-only">for-one-night-only</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer182735361" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10410818761797303979">Art, paint, glass, energy, romance, color, and so, so many secrets are all splashed, swirled and exhibited on the pages of Graffiti Moon. For one night, we learn to look and really see the night through artisits’ eyes. A colorful night filled with celebrating and shadow hunting.<br/><br/>O’ the colors! The colors jumped out at me from the pages of this book right away. Gray buildings, yellow birds, “the exact kind of blue”, black night, pink vans, clear glass, white oceans, and the reds, greens, and orang</span>
  <span id="freeText10410818761797303979" style="display:none">Art, paint, glass, energy, romance, color, and so, so many secrets are all splashed, swirled and exhibited on the pages of Graffiti Moon. For one night, we learn to look and really see the night through artisits’ eyes. A colorful night filled with celebrating and shadow hunting.<br /><br />O’ the colors! The colors jumped out at me from the pages of this book right away. Gray buildings, yellow birds, “the exact kind of blue”, black night, pink vans, clear glass, white oceans, and the reds, greens, and oranges on the canvases and glass! The sound and feel of these colors wake you up! They bring the words and characters to life. <br /><br />We are introduced to such an energetic, creative, and smart band of individuals with just a “wanker” or two thrown into the mix for good measure. All filled with hurt, confusion, and emotion so powerful at times they just have to say what’s in their heads in glass, paint or poetry to get it out.<br /><br />“Paint sails and the things that kick in my head scream from the can to brick.”<br /><br />I adored them all—Lucy, Ed, Leo, Jazz, Daisy, Dylan, Al, Bert, and so many more. How they all moved, interacted, and learned from each other was an inspirational key to the story for me.<br /><br />Lucy is a strong, smart, beautiful, confident, give-it-right-back-to-ya type of girl. Needless to say, I loved Lucy right from the first swing of her elbow! Ed was heartbreakingly lost, but still searching--hidden but screaming out at the same time. You just had to know where to look to find him and Lucy was looking. Their sharp edged, witty banter and chemistry pushed the night along with such energy. It flowed. They made me laugh and smile. They even made one of my favorite hand gestures fun and flirty! :) <br /><br />One message I took to heart from the pages was the power and influence of paying attention. This book is filled with examples of mentoring and inspiration--Al tutoring Lucy’s love and admiration for glassblowing, Miss J influencing her students in the classroom and out, Ed’s Mom buying Leo a bed, and Bert taking the time to make an impact in Ed’s life by talking and listening. Look up and find inspiration in the sky, a face, smile, freckle, or voice. Just noticing the colors around you, splashed up on the walls or in nature can make a difference in you or perhaps someone else’s life. <br /><br />Inspiration. Every artist needs it. We all do.<br /><br />I highly recommend this book. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10410818761797303979" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_181053122" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/181053122" />
    <a title="Reynje" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5590906-reynje"><img alt="Reynje" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473722441p2/5590906.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/181053122?book_show_action=true">Jul 01, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Reynje" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Reynje" href="/user/show/5590906-reynje">Reynje</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer181053122" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17097782354257983040">I’m going to preface this review with a warning that I find it hard to talk about this book without gushing - an urge that has not diminished with each subsequent reading. I'm not sure how to sufficiently express how much I adore this book, so I may just start flinging adjectives wildly as I go on. Sorry. <br/><br/>Taking place over one unseasonably hot night in Melbourne, Graffiti Moon is a story about art, poetry and love. About secret identities, past mistakes and punches in the face. About pink vans a</span>
  <span id="freeText17097782354257983040" style="display:none">I’m going to preface this review with a warning that I find it hard to talk about this book without gushing - an urge that has not diminished with each subsequent reading. I'm not sure how to sufficiently express how much I adore this book, so I may just start flinging adjectives wildly as I go on. Sorry. <br /><br />Taking place over one unseasonably hot night in Melbourne, Graffiti Moon is a story about art, poetry and love. About secret identities, past mistakes and punches in the face. About pink vans and an elusive perfect shade of blue. And a girl on a mission to find Shadow, a graffiti artist who documents his thoughts on walls around the city. <br /><br />Crowley weaves the plot together through the perspectives of Ed and Lucy, two unique, nuanced teenage voices, interspersed with the works of Poet as the night unfolds. A slight overlap between some scenes allows you to see how the same events are filtered by each of the protagonists, and watch as the relationships between them develop and change. The interactions between the characters were refreshingly realistic: Dylan and Daisy’s barbed exchanges, Ed’s caution, Lucy’s unfiltered observations. I loved them all. Flawed but charming boys, girls with style and strength. Chemistry that fizzes from the page. <br /><br />A story by turns funny and poignant, Crowley’s prose is lyrical yet understated. The writing is evocative, pulling you in and immersing you in the story. Its an experience not unlike the way Ed describes a Rothko painting: “.. for a while, as long as you’re looking at it, that painting is the world and you get to be in it.” (p 167). Graffiti Moon is the type of book that holds you close, wrapping you up in the tension, until the final page. <br /><br />I particularly enjoyed the discussion and use of art throughout the book, from references to local artists Ghostpatrol and Angela Brennan, to the ongoing motif of Rene Magritte’s The Lovers in Lucy’s point of view. I’ll be the first to admit I know next to nothing about art, but I found the use in the story both relatable and effective. <br /><br />Also, the shout outs to Melbourne’s street art really made me want to go out and rediscover the city I live in :)<br /><br />Graffiti Moon in a gorgeous book that captures the hopefulness and uncertainty of standing on the brink of your future. <br /><br />It now has a permanent spot as one of my favourite reads of all time. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17097782354257983040" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
